        <p class="date">
         Wed Jan 18, 2012 at 08:30 PM PST
        </p>
        <h2>
         <a href="/story/2012/01/19/1056076/-Open-Thread-for-Night-Owls-SOPA-the-MPAA-and-Chris-Dodd" id="titleHref">
          Open Thread for Night Owls: SOPA, the MPAA and Chris Dodd
         </a>
         <span style="white-space: nowrap">
         </span>
        </h2>
        <p class="author">
         <span>
          by
         </span>
         <a href="/user/Hunter">
          Hunter
         </a>
         <a alt="Follow this author" class="ajax type-user do-hotlist do-updateContent size-tiny off altTooltip" href="#?friend_id=1054&amp;is_stream=1">
          Follow
         </a>
         <span class="for">
          for
         </span>
         <a href="/blog/main">
          Daily Kos
         </a>
        </p>
        <ul class="front-page-share clearfix">
         <li style="margin-left: 0px">
          <div class="fb-share-button" data-href="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2012/01/19/1056076/-Open-Thread-for-Night-Owls-SOPA-the-MPAA-and-Chris-Dodd" data-layout="button_count">
          </div>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="twitter-share-button" data-count="horizontal" data-related="markos" data-text="Open Thread for Night Owls: SOPA, the MPAA and Chris Dodd" data-url="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2012/01/19/1056076/-Open-Thread-for-Night-Owls-SOPA-the-MPAA-and-Chris-Dodd" data-via="dailykos" href="https://twitter.com/share">
           Tweet
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="comments comment_count_with_new" data-comment_count="193" data-story_id="1056076" href="/story/2012/01/19/1056076/-Open-Thread-for-Night-Owls-SOPA-the-MPAA-and-Chris-Dodd#comments">
           193 Comments
          </a>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </div>
       <div class="article-body">
        <div id="intro">
         <div class="dkimg-c">
          <img alt="Open Thread for Night Owls" height="106" src="http://images1.dailykos.com/i/user/1054/sopa_owl.jpg" width="550"/>
         </div>
         For as long as I can remember, the MPAA (that's Motion Picture Association of America) has labored hard in their effort to be the most universally reviled industry group in the country. They are in stiff competition with the music business, but still manage to hold their own. What makes both these groups special is their ability to treat absolutely everyone like dirt: directors, actors, artists, distributers, consumers, everyone. To hear the MPAA tell it, the entire world revolves around a handful of companies whose content comes to them via magical pixie delivery service, the only talent that exists in the world is Studio Head, and everyone else from actors to consumers to the person playing bass guitar is a filthy, valueless leech only tolerated because slavery is still technically prohibited (for now). My own expectation is that there's something in the water, but in any event, in order to work there you have to be a raging, insufferable asshole with a titanic ego and no apparent skills other than raw parasitism.
         <p>
          Enter former Sen. Chris Dodd.
         </p>
         <p>
          As Markos
          <a href="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2012/01/17/1055719/-MPAAs-statement-on-internet-blackout?via=search">
           already mentioned
          </a>
          , the only substantial response from the MPAA to the SOPA/PIPA internet blackout has come in the form of a
          <em>
           profoundly
          </em>
          pompous statement penned by Chris Dodd, or at least penned by an army of soulless half-humans in an MPAA lab,
          <a href="http://www.hollywoodreporter.com/news/mpaa-chris-dodd-blackout-piracy-sopa-282755">
           then signed by Chris Dodd afterwards
          </a>
          .
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          MPAA Chairman Chris Dodd came out swinging Tuesday in the fight over pending Internet anti-piracy legislation calling online web sites and tech companies supporting the Blackout Day protest scheduled for Wednesday irresponsible and calling their protest action a disservice to people who rely on them for information or use their services.
          <p>
           It is also an abuse of power given the freedoms these companies enjoy in the marketplace today, said Dodd in a statement. Its a dangerous and troubling development when the platforms that serve as gateways to information intentionally skew the facts to incite their users in order to further their corporate interests.
          </p>
         </blockquote>
         <p>
          Yes, Markos already hit it. But I get to hit it again, under the This is So Stupid It Deserves Constant Mention rule. For starters: the sheer arrogance of the statement. That's not accidental, that is how the entertainment industry trade groups present themselves in nearly every situation. If a Girl Scout goes up to the head of the MPAA, she won't get away again until she hears how her very existence is only allowed because the big corporate studios make it possible, and that the color green is a copyright infringement, and that selling cookies is prohibited because cookies are a form of entertainment and fuck you, little girl, for thinking you could do that without handing over a large cut of the profits.
         </p>
         <p>
          The sole argument Dodd has here is this, and I'm not kidding: You, internet websites, are engaged in an "abuse of power" by taking down your own websites. Only the MPAA gets to decide when to take down
          <em>
           your
          </em>
          websites. So shut up.
         </p>
         <p>
          That's what the whole law is about: giving the largest entertainment companies themselves the right to preemptively shut down any effing website they want, under unproven claims of "infringement", and leaving it to the poor pisser on the other side to try to prove their innocence in court battles after the fact. And why shouldn't they try for that? We are for the most part there already, after all; Congress has steadily been ceding government authority and mandating court deference to private industries over and over again, so getting it over with and just letting a top handful of companies preemptively decide who they think might be breaking the law, then giving them heightened government-assisted abilities to destroy the "offender" in question
          <em>
           before
          </em>
          actually having to prove their casewell, that seems like a logical next step, doesn't it? The true genius of it, however, is the added bonus of being able to threaten any internet site that even has a
          <em>
           link
          </em>
          to the supposed offender, or that allows users to post content that is not properly pre-censored to remove "potential" copyright claims according to whatever guessed criteria these companies later come up with. If the MPAA decides you haven't been taking explicit steps to "confirm" that no users or commenters are posting things it deems naughty, that's it: you're shut down as well. That's the real kicker, the call for preemptive, universal monitoring of
          <em>
           all
          </em>
          posted internet content. Forget the technical incompetence of the bill; the intent and logic alone is a megacorporate fantasy come to life. Preemptive shutdowns! Seizing assets! A required level of user policing that is objectively
          <em>
           impossible
          </em>
          for most sites to reasonably meet (including, hilariously,
          <a href="http://deadspin.com/5877322/">
           the sites of the MPAA-belonging, SOPA-supporting studios themselves, you unrelenting dipshits
          </a>
          ), thereby ensuring a rich and unending stream of new criminals!
         </p>
         <p>
          You can practically hear the condescension dripping from Dodd's statement, the
          <em>
           outrage
          </em>
          that these silly internet companies are still able to express themselves in any way at all, if that expression comes in a form that might slightly inconvenience Sony, or Disney, or whatever other entertainment mega-corporation wants the power to literally police the entire
          <em>
           structure
          </em>
          of the internet in the name of their supposed corporate rights.
         </p>
         <p>
          Oh, I think we're all for reducing piracy. As shown by their unwillingness to just change their flawed and asinine bill already, however, the MPAA, like the music industry, is not quite so narrowly targeted on that. Their more pressing concern has of late been how to continue to squeeze top profits out of a distribution model that increasingly does not need them, and doesn't want them, and which revolves around bleeding content producers and consumers both, and that, in turn, requires tight control over every other possible means of alternate distribution (see: Net Neutrality, the fight over whether or not many of these same companies should be able to charge you a steeper fee if you get your content from "discouraged" sources, i.e. competitors, critics, or anyone else who makes it onto their corporate blacklist).
         </p>
         <p>
          If it were easier to buy content, people would do more of it (iTunes, etc., has begun to help in this regard for music, but the film and television industries will apparently have to be dragged kicking and screaming into the electronic age). If industry groups did not consistently and absurdly overstep in what they called "infringement," and so had a small bit more credibility in this debate, that would help too. While we're at it we can ponder on the Neverending Copyright Story, the constant battle to ensure that we treat corporate copyrights as infinite entities, more sacrosanct than the original artist-centric version ever was, because once again corporate giants
          <em>
           of course
          </em>
          deserve stronger protection than individual people. That's just
          <em>
           natural
          </em>
          .
         </p>
         <p>
          Net Un-Neutrality, SOPA, PIPA and ever-expanding copyright laws; a ridiculous patent system; ALEC, the MPAA, the Keystone fight; the legal fights over fracking; the mere political existence of Mitt Romney: Every aspect of our current government is predicated on expanding corporate power, and if that power conflicts with deeper American principles than those other principles can piss off. Even while we celebrate the internet bringing concrete benefits to other nations, we seek to limit it at home because some group of lobbyists says that corporate profits demand it. Then we have to listen to those same corporate voices condemn us for having the rotten audacity to even
          <em>
           object
          </em>
          .
         </p>
         <p>
          <br/>
         </p>
         <hr color="#000099" size="2" width="75%"/>
         <p>
          <a href="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2005/01/18/86265/-Florida-DNC-members-endorse-Dean-en-masse?detail=hide&amp;via=blog_1">
           Blast from the Past
          </a>
          . At Daily Kos on this date in
          <b>
           2005
          </b>
          :
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          The Florida delegation to the Democratic National Committee has voted unanimously to endorse Howard Dean to be the party's next chairman, bucking an effort to orchestrate an endorsement of one candidate by all 50 state party leaders at the same time later this month.
          <p>
           The decision, announced yesterday by Scott Maddox, the Florida Democratic chairman, is a major lift for Dr. Dean, a former governor of Vermont, and it is a shift in a contest where most Democrats have been holding back from endorsing any candidate in the crowded field.
          </p>
          <p>
           Mr. Maddox said in an interview that Florida made its endorsement despite some Democrats' concerns that Dr. Dean might not be the right ideological symbol for the party as it tries to regain power because of his liberal views on some issues and fervent opposition to the Iraq war.
          </p>
          <p>
           "The only knock against Howard Dean is that he's seen as too liberal," Mr. Maddox said. "I'm a gun-owning pickup-truck driver and I have a bulldog named Lockjaw. I am a Southern chairman of a Southern state, and I am perfectly comfortable with Howard Dean as D.N.C. chair."
           <br/>
          </p>
         </blockquote>
         <hr color="#000099" size="2" width="75%"/>

       <div class="tags">

         <p>
          Add keywords that describe this diary.
		Separate multiple keywords with commas.
          <br/>
          <a href="/special/tag_tips" target="_blank">
           Tagging tips
          </a>
          -
          <a href="/search?search_tags=1" target="_blank">
           Search For Tags
          </a>
          -
          <a href="http://www.dkosopedia.com/wiki/Tag:Tagfinder" target="_blank">

         <div class="tooltipContents qtip-style-dk4_large qtip-pos-br">
          <p>
           <b>
            More Tagging tips:
           </b>
          </p>
          <p>
           A tag is a way to search for this diary. If someone is searching for "Barack Obama," is this a diary they'd be trying to find?
          </p>
          <p>
           Use a person's full name, without any title. Senator Obama may become President Obama, and Michelle Obama might run for office.
          </p>
          <p>
           If your diary covers an election or elected official, use election tags, which are generally the state abbreviation followed by the office. 
		CA-01 is the first district House seat. CA-Sen covers both senate races. NY-GOV covers the New York governor's race.
          </p>
          <p>
           Tags do not compound: that is, "education reform" is a completely different tag from "education". A tag like "reform" alone is probably not meaningful.
          </p>
         </div>
         <!-- &lt;h4 id="p_tagErrorMessage"&gt;You must enter at least one Tag for this Diary Entry:&lt;/h4&gt; -->
         <p>
          <input id="p_tagInput" name="tag_draft" size="70" type="text" value=""/>
          <!-- &lt;input id="tagSubmit" type="submit" name="submit" value="Submit" /&gt; -->
         </p>
         <p style="font-style:italic">
          Consider if one or more of these tags fits your diary:
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Civil Rights');return false;">
           Civil Rights
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Community');return false;">
           Community
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Congress');return false;">
           Congress
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Culture');return false;">
           Culture
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Economy');return false;">
           Economy
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Education');return false;">
           Education
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Elections');return false;">
           Elections
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Energy');return false;">
           Energy
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Environment');return false;">
           Environment
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Health Care');return false;">
           Health Care
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('International');return false;">
           International
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Labor');return false;">
           Labor
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Law');return false;">
           Law
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Media');return false;">
           Media
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Meta');return false;">
           Meta
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('National Security');return false;">
           National Security
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Science');return false;">
           Science
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Transportation');return false;">
           Transportation
          </a>
          , or
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('White House');return false;">
           White House
          </a>
          .
	If your diary is specific to a state, consider adding the state 
	(
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('California');return false;">
           California
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Texas');return false;">
           Texas
          </a>
          , etc).
	Keep in mind, though, that there are many wonderful and important diaries
	that don't fit in any of these tags. Don't worry if yours doesn't.
         </p>

              </p>
              <p class="cb">
               by
               <a href="/user/uid:155717">
                rebel ga
               </a>
               on
               <a href="/comments/1056076/44643831#c150">

         <li id="c145">
          <div class="cx" id="cx44643766">
           <h5>
            <a class="de">
            </a>
            <span class="cu">
             I'm going to look now Eddie.
            </span>
            <span class="crd ntb">
             (
             <a href="/comments/1056076/44643766#c145?mode=alone;showrate=1#c145">
              1+ / 0-
             </a>
             )
            </span>
           </h5>
           <div class="crs">
            <dl>
             <dt>
              Recommended by:
             </dt>
             <dd>
              <a href="/user/uid:37228">
               riverlover
              </a>
             </dd>
            </dl>
           </div>
           <div class="ct">
            <p>
             I wasn't sure exactly what MPAA stood for so I googled it.
             <strong>
              <em>
               The Major Studios
              </em>
             </strong>
             <a href="http://www.mpaa.org/about/ceo">
              The Motion Picture Association of America
             </a>
            </p>
            <p>
             I understand about movie piracy.
             <strong>
              <em>
               Although why anyone would want to watch half of them I have no idea.
              </em>
             </strong>
             Special effects gone wild, loud in your face kind of stuff. It's no wonder so many young people are on drugs and alcohol!
            </p>
            <p>
             I have been in disagreement with the movie studio's cheaply made movie policies for at least, over 30 years!
            </p>
            <p>
             The republicans don't have to control the minds of the young, the media already does!
             <strong>
              <em>
               Or is that the same thing nowadays?
              </em>
             </strong>
            </p>
            <p>
             People; (young, impressionable ones especially,
             <em>
              voice of experience here
             </em>
             ), are forming their opinions by repeated exposure to violence, for one very important thing!
            </p>
            <p>
             Why can't movies be entertaining and educational as well!
            </p>
            <p>
             We've come so far forward in America in the past 100 years and now they're trying to pull us backwards!
            </p>
            <p>
             Back in the 1930's when gangsters were idolized in those old simply photographed black and white films. That kind of crime was elevated in society.
            </p>
            <p>
             Now it's a shoot em, up violent genre of movies again, (with assorted bad guys) only now in big screen cinema scope, (or whatever they're using nowadays)!
            </p>
            <p>
             There is a correlation between these kinds of violence in movies and media, and of that kind of behavior on the streets of the US! Of course poverty is the main cause, but accepted violence in the media only suggests that this is the way people can solve their issues. i e The Killing Cycle: Inside story of the Essex County homicide squad
             <a href="http://www.nj.com/news/index.ssf/2011/08/essex_county_homicide_squad_in.html">
              as it tries to break the murder chain
             </a>
             <em>
              by Mark Di Ionno/Star-Ledger Columnist
             </em>
             Sunday, August 14 2011
            </p>
            <p>
             The studios choose the movies.
             <em>
              And what's with those video games?
             </em>
             I think they're pirated too. Again, most should only be sold to 18 and over and even then I think playing them 24/7 could have a mind numbing affect. Although; unlike movies that get into your mind, some video games might be relatively stress relieving.
            </p>
            <p>
             I don't think that even the music industry makes enough money for too much thievery to be profitable.
            </p>
            <p>
             I don't understand why promoting this internet protection act was necessary to begin with. Because
             <strong>
              I don't see any evidence that the internet could be where pirating is going on at all.
             </strong>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              The internet is already well policed by the websites.
             </strong>
             i e I know if I have a video and it's not legit, soon it's gone and no longer embeddable.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              So is SOPA a ploy for the movie industry to get more power? Or is it an attempt to control the media?
              <em>
               Both probably.
              </em>
             </strong>
            </p>
            <blockquote>
             <strong>
              Last Chance
             </strong>
             <a href="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2012/01/13/1054411/-Last-Chance-To-Try-And-%E2%99%A5Save-This-Soap%E2%99%A5?via=history">
              To Try And
             </a>
             <strong>
              <em>
               
              </em>
              Save This Soap
              <em>
               
              </em>
             </strong>
             <em>
              No relation to SOPA
             </em>
             <p>
              <strong>
               I just love these guys, they're so cute.
               <em>
                There's no business, like show business!
               </em>
              </strong>
              <br/>
              <iframe defang_allowfullscreen="" frameborder="0" height="315" src="http://www.youtube.com/embed/mDv4PibAf-o?rel=0" width="420">
              </iframe>
             </p>
            </blockquote>
            <p>
             <strong>
              I rec'd this diary.
             </strong>
            </p>

              <p>
               I don't agree with it, but I can kind of understand Boxer and Feinstein selling out their huge technology industry. It's BS because they're preferring SoCal and entertainment over NoCal and technology, but at least they have some sort of rationale.
              </p>
              <p>
               But virtually every film and tv show "set in" Washington is produced/filmed in BC. How nice it would have been if all the Twilight movies were filmed in Forks, on the Peninsula and in our state. That could have provided a lot of people with work; a lot of businesses with income.
              </p>
              <p>
               When the entertainment industry came asking, she should have suggested they go to the BC parliament building and ask for votes there. I have nothing against BC and our Canuck friends, btw. This industry exports these jobs, driving straight through our state to do so, but wants our senators to vote for them to protect their rights with overreaching oppressive bills?
              </p>
              <p>
               What's wrong with this picture?

          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            the bill to make Martin Luther King, Jr. Day a federal holiday passed in 1983. It passed the House 338-90, and then the Senate 78-22.
           </p>
           <p>
            The question is, do you know who voted against it back in 1983 that's still in Congress to this day? There were 9 House members who voted against it who are still serving in Congress today (note: they may not all be necessarily still in the House, hint, hint), and there are two Senators out of the 22 who voted against it that are still serving today.
           </p>
           <p>
            Without looking it up, who are they?
           </p>
           <p>
            From Monday's responses, y'all have gotten the following:
           </p>
           <p>
            House: John McCain (AZ), Ron Paul (TX)
            <br/>
            Senate: Orrin Hatch (UT)
           </p>
           <p>
            There's still 7 others who were in the House in 1983 that are still in Congress today (not necessarily still in the House, mind you), and another Senator.
           </p>

                   less
                  </strong>
                  blood and gore regardless of how much shooting and bombing and explosions directors show. So kids don't learn that violence has truly awful consequences.
                 </p>
                 <p>
                  He says that if the movie accurately shows how obscenly bloody and destructive violence is, give it a G or PG rating. If it shows the sanitized version of violence, give it an R. The whole system needs to be flipped over because right now, our youngest kids don't learn that guns and bombs actually hurt people.
                 </p>
                 <p>
                  Then we sit on the sidelines and complain that kids are dulled to violence. Yeah, there's some of that, especially -- I think -- in video game players. But pay attention to how often people are shot and there's little or no blood, certainly, no flying gray matter (or other body parts), and how often people survive direct hits.
                 </p>
                 <p>
                  Do I want this stuff beamed into my living room? No. But you couldn't pay me to watch stuff like
                  <em>
                   Criminal Minds
                  </em>
                  anyhow. If it were more realistic, perhaps many other Americans would realize what a truly, obscenely violent show it is and object as well-- or at the very least, not let their kids and teens anywhere near it.
                 </p>
                </div>
                <div class="cf">
                 <p class="sig">
                   grover
                 </p>
                 <hr color="#6600CC" size="4" width="40%"/>
                 So if you get hit by a bus tonight, would you be satisfied with how you spent today, your last day on earth? Live like tomorrow is never guaranteed, because it's not.
                 <p class="cb">
                  by
                  <a href="/user/uid:16053">
                   grover
                  </a>
                  on
                  <a href="/comments/1056076/44648855#c187">
                   Thu Jan 19, 2012 at 10:58:36 AM PST
                  </a>
                 </p>

                  <a href="#c184">

                  </a>

                 </p>
                </div>

          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            <strong>
             HAIL and FAREWELL
            </strong>
            to the singer, songwriter, drummer, bandleader and disc jockey
            <a href="http://www.thestate.com/2012/01/18/v-print/2119468/johnny-otis-rb-singer-who-wrote.html">
             Johnny Otis
            </a>
            who has died at the age of 90. He was inducted into the Rock &amp; Roll
            <a href="http://rockhall.com/inductees/johnny-otis/bio/">
             Hall of Fame
            </a>
            in 1994 but he charted just one crossover hit in his career: 1958s
            <em>
             Willie and the Hand Jive,
            </em>
            a salty R&amp;B novelty later covered by Eric Clapton and others.
           </p>
          </div>

           <div class="ct">
            <p>
             so I went and checked my profile. I have way more comment ratings than comments made so I'm assuming it's one of two possible things. First, and most likely it's the number of comments that I have given a rating to or the other possibility is the accumulated ratings on the old 0 to 4 rating system. I doubt it's the 2nd option.
            </p>
            <p>
             I have 21,492 comments made (93 with this one) and 119,730 comment ratings. IMO those are the comments I have rated. Could be wrong.
            </p>

              If you go to your stream page, there's a tab for "comment ratings."

          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            Sick of asshole Dodd. This bastard did the vile bidding of the securities and insurance industries, to the severe detriment of all Americans. No surprise hedge fund scam artists reside en mass in Greenwich, Connecticut.
           </p>
           <p>
            Oh, and for a good read on these scumbag hedge funds, give a read to
            <a href="http://www.bloomberg.com/news/2012-01-18/hedge-funds-buy-ferraris-clients-often-get-phantom-gain-books.html">
             Hedge Funds Buy Ferraris With Phantom Profits, Leave Clients with Crumbs
            </a>
            . An excerpt:
           </p>
           <blockquote>
            From 1998 through 2010 . . . "real investor profits" totaled $70 billion, compared with fees of $379 billion, Lack estimates. Adding the fees back in, hedge fund managers salted away 84 percent of $449 billion in total profits, leaving 16 percent for their investors, he says.
            <p>
             And that's not the worst of it, Lack says. HFRX index doesn't account for factors such as "survivor bias," meaning that only surviving hedge funds report returns (just as the victors write history, he says). Adjusting for those biases, the annual fees sink to $324 billion, while the real investor profits plunge to a negative $308 billion, he says.
            </p>
            <p>
             Consider, too, the fees charged by funds of hedge funds, used by roughly a third of hedge-fund investors, Lack says. Throwing that into the mix, investors were left with $9 billion, while the industry amassed $440 billion in fees, or 98 percent.
            </p>
           </blockquote>
          </div>

            The Louis CK Model
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1056076/44643182#c90?mode=alone;showrate=1#c90">
             6+ / 0-
            </a>

          <div class="crs">

             </a>

          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            Louis CK self-financed his latest special and sold it for $5 a pop. It cost him about $200,000 and he broke even in about a day. Also, because all the money went directly to the artist, users of torrent sites were more hesitant to pirate it (there was hostility by a lot of users to say the least). He detailed the whole process in an email you received after purchase which had this awesome quote in it;
           </p>
           <p>
            'I learned that money can be a lot of things. It can be something that is hoarded, fought over, protected, stolen and withheld. Or it can be like an energy, fueled by the desire, will, creative interest, need to laugh, of large groups of people. And it can be shuffled and pushed around and pooled together to fuel a common interest, jokes about garbage, penises and parenthood.' -Louis CK
           </p>

        <li id="c140">
         <div class="cx" id="cx44643708">
          <h5>
           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            To understand the MPAA, you have to understand the
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1056076/44643708#c140?mode=alone;showrate=1#c140">
             2+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="crs">
           <dl>
            <dt>
             Recommended by:
            </dt>
            <dd>
             <a href="/user/uid:231987">
              Eric Nelson
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:2886">
              hannah
             </a>
            </dd>
           </dl>
          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            <strong>
             term "rent" as a technical economic concept.
            </strong>
           </p>
           <p>
            It's the value of goods or services, beyond the cost of production, that is endowed by the exclusivity of of the product.
           </p>
           <p>
            A good oil well produces value many times the cost of exploration, drilling and pumping. Economists call that value "rent". The recipients of that value are "rentiers".
           </p>
           <p>
            The MPAA exists mainly to protect the rent value of entertainment products... by protecting their exclusivity.
           </p>
           <p>
            Each work of cinema is, to them, an "oil well" that keeps on pumping revenue long after it's production costs have been recouped, with a tidy profit, or even an obscene profit.
           </p>
           <p>
            Rentiers contribute nothing to the economy, they're just taxing the consumer because the law entitles them to do so.
           </p>
           <p>
           </p>
          </div>

             Middlemen are parasites. They take from both sides.
             <br/>
             In a sense they compete with our public entities. That's why the chamber of commerce which represents the interests of the middlemen are antagonistic towards any tax. They perceive taxes as a reduction on their 'cut.'

             In a sense, the creative destruction practiced by Romney and his ilk is part of the artificial scarcity creation process. The parasite got rich and then they god greedy and killed the golden goose.

        <li id="c160">
         <div class="cx" id="cx44643967">
          <h5>
           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            Dear Andrew Sullivan
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1056076/44643967#c160?mode=alone;showrate=1#c160">
             3+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="crs">
           <dl>
            <dt>
             Recommended by:
            </dt>
            <dd>
             <a href="/user/uid:22212">
              Agathena
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:46817">
              Alexander G Rubio
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:56197">
              Tommy Allen
             </a>
            </dd>
           </dl>
          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            <a href="http://www.theatlantic.com/politics/archive/2012/01/dear-andrew-sullivan-why-focus-on-obamas-dumbest-critics/251528/">
             Dear Andrew Sullivan: Why Focus on Obama's Dumbest Critics?
            </a>
           </p>
           <blockquote>
            After reading Andrew Sullivan's Newsweek essay about President Obama, his critics, and his re-election bid, I implore him to ponder just one question. How would you have reacted in 2008 if any Republican ran promising to do the following?
            <blockquote>
             (1) Codify indefinite detention into law; (2) draw up a secret kill list of people, including American citizens, to assassinate without due process; (3) proceed with warrantless spying on American citizens; (4) prosecute Bush-era whistleblowers for violating state secrets; (5) reinterpret the War Powers Resolution such that entering a war of choice without a Congressional declaration is permissible; (6) enter and prosecute such a war; (7) institutionalize naked scanners and intrusive full body pat-downs in major American airports; (8) oversee a planned expansion of TSA so that its agents are already beginning to patrol American highways, train stations, and bus depots; (9) wage an undeclared drone war on numerous Muslim countries that delegates to the CIA the final call about some strikes that put civilians in jeopardy; (10) invoke the state-secrets privilege to dismiss lawsuits brought by civil-liberties organizations on dubious technicalities rather than litigating them on the merits; (11) preside over federal raids on medical marijuana dispensaries; (12) attempt to negotiate an extension of American troops in Iraq beyond 2011 (an effort that thankfully failed); (14) reauthorize the Patriot Act; (13) and select an economic team mostly made up of former and future financial executives from Wall Street firms that played major roles in the financial crisis.
            </blockquote>
           </blockquote>
           <p>
            It's pretty pathetic to see some on this and other sites giving more credence to a right winger like Andrew Sullivan who's actually voted Republican in the past than to a progressive like Chris Hedges who some have now labeled as a right wing hack.
           </p>

          <h5>
           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            Explaining SOPA
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1056076/44644068#c166?mode=alone;showrate=1#c166">
             0+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            Yesterday had to be an outstanding success, from the number of middle-roaders who asked me to explain it to them. When I explained that a small site manager could never have the resources to prevent all infringement, and therefore the small sites would be doomed without due process, I got universal agreement that the law was stupid.
           </p>

        <li id="c167">
         <div class="cx" id="cx44644120">
          <h5>
           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            Bracing for pie fight, but must speak op IP
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1056076/44644120#c167?mode=alone;showrate=1#c167">
             2+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="crs">
           <dl>
            <dt>
             Recommended by:
            </dt>
            <dd>
             <a href="/user/uid:322874">
              joe wobblie
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:111628">
              JeffW
             </a>
            </dd>
           </dl>
          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            Disclaimer: TheGrandWazoo has a financial interest in intellectual property protection.
           </p>
           <p>
            Claim: TheGrandWazoo does not believe that this interest has had a skewing effect on TheGrandWazoo's thoughts as follows:
           </p>
           <p>
            Due to my above stated financial interest, I will not take a stand on the merits of SOPA or PIPA in this forum. However I would like to point out the following:
           </p>
           <p>
            It is heartbreakingly difficult for songwriters to make a living creating the music they love to make and that we love to hear. Most songwriters are lucky to have one success, and most do not perform their own music; even recognition is often denied to them as stars bask in the glory of songs written by others. The only source of income they derive from their creative work comes from that which is guaranteed and protected by copyright law.
           </p>
           <p>
            There is a constant drumbeat on commentary on how the music industry treats songwriters and performers like crap. Let's take that as a given. The question is what is a greater priority, clobbering the villains or saving the victims. If you sink a slave ship, the captives go down with the crew.
           </p>
           <p>
            Again, I am not taking a stand on SOPA or PIPA here. But I am taking a stand for the individuals who try to create, and deserve a chance to make a living doing so. This chance should
            <strong>
             not
            </strong>
            come at the price of censorship, but absolute freedom of speech should not come at the price of this chance.
           </p>
          </div>
          <div class="cf">
           <p class="sig">

           </p>
           <blockquote>
            ...described the blackout protest as an irresponsible response and accused those taking part of intentionally [skewing] the facts.
            <p>
             A so-called blackout is yet another gimmick, albeit a dangerous one, designed to punish elected and administration officials who are working diligently to protect American jobs from foreign criminals, Dodd added. It is our hope that the White House and the Congress will call on those who intend to stage this blackout to stop the hyperbole and PR stunts and engage in meaningful efforts to combat piracy.
            </p>
           </blockquote>
          </div>
          <div class="cf">
           <p class="sig">
            <em>
             "...just ordinary people, you know, people who are not famous, if they get together, if they persist, if they defy the authorities, they can defeat the largest corporation in the world. - Howard Zinn
            </em>
           </p>
           <p class="cb">
            by
            <a href="/user/uid:325015">
             Sean X
            </a>
            on
            <a href="/comments/1056076/44644683#c179">
             Thu Jan 19, 2012 at 05:56:56 AM PST
            </a>
           </p>
           <p class="cl">
           </p>
          </div>
         </div>
        </li>
        <li id="c185">
         <div class="cx" id="cx44645939">
          <h5>
           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            Would you say that the NDAA
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1056076/44645939#c185?mode=alone;showrate=1#c185">
             0+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            which allows unfettered abuse of citizens by the military and executive branch is in this as well?
           </p>
           <blockquote>
            Every aspect of our current government is predicated on expanding corporate power, and if that power conflicts with deeper American principles than those other principles can piss off. Even while we celebrate the internet bringing concrete benefits to other nations, we seek to limit it at home because some group of lobbyists says that corporate profits demand it. Then we have to listen to those same corporate voices condemn us for having the rotten audacity to even object.
           </blockquote>
          </div>
          <div class="cf">
           <p class="sig">
            Congress is at 9% approval rating - within the +/- of making herpes more popular than congress! - Webranding
           </p>
           <p class="cb">
            by
            <a href="/user/uid:5137">
             glitterscale
            </a>
            on
            <a href="/comments/1056076/44645939#c185">
             Thu Jan 19, 2012 at 07:39:25 AM PST
            </a>
           </p>
           <p class="cl">
           </p>
          </div>
         </div>
        </li>

  <script type="text/javascript">
   if (document.location.pathname.match(/^\/story/)) {
			  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Story', {  url: "http://www.dailykos.com/story/2012/01/19/1056076/-Open-Thread-for-Night-Owls-SOPA-the-MPAA-and-Chris-Dodd", 
			                                            blog: "main",

  </script>
  <script type="text/javascript">
   if($.cookie('meter_user') !== 'false') {
		if ($('#ePostButton').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('#ePostButton').click(function() { 
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Posted Comment', { 
		      repliedTo: $(this).parents('#eP').prevAll('.cb').children('a').first().html() 
		    });
		  });
		}
		
		if (!!document.location.pathname.match('activate') &amp;&amp; $('h1:contains("Welcome to Daily Kos!")').length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Signed Up');
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname === '/') {
		  if (document.location.hostname.match(/^www|^dailykos/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Front Page');
		  } else {
		    var subdomain = document.location.hostname.split('.')[0];
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Vertical', { name: subdomain });
		  }
		}
		
		if ($('.ratinate').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.ratinate').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Recommended Comment') });
		}
		
		if ($('.do-addRating.type-story').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.do-addRating.type-story').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Recommended Story') });
		}
		
		if ($("form[action$='publishHow']").length &gt; 0) {
		  $(document).ready(function() {
			  $('.type-story.do-publishHow').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Published Story') });
			 });
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname.match(/^\/user/) &amp;&amp; $('li.here').length &gt; 0) {
		  if ($('.pageMenu:first li.here').children('a').html().match(/Stream/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Stream', { name: $('.name').children('a').html() });
		  } else if ($('.pageMenu:first li.here').children('a').html().match(/Profile/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Profile', { name: $('.name').children('a').html() });
		  } else if ($('.pageMenu:last li.here').children('a').html().match(/My Recent Replies/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Replies');
		  }
		} 
		
		if ($('#search-tabbed').length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Searched');
		}
		
		if ($('#group-tables').length &gt; 0) {
			DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Groups List');
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname.match(/^\/groups/) &amp;&amp; $("#group_info").length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Group', { name: $('.name').children('a').text() });
		}
		
		if ($('.do-hotlist.type-user, .do-unHotlist.type-user').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.do-hotlist.type-user, .do-unHotlist.type-user').click(function() {
		    var nickName;
		    nickName = ($(this).prev('a').html() || $('.name a').html())
		    if ($(this).hasClass('do-hotlist')) {
		      DailyKos.Metrics.track('Followed User', { nickname: nickName }) 
		    } else if ($(this).hasClass('do-unHotlist')) {
		      DailyKos.Metrics.track('Unfollowed User', { nickname: nickName }) 
		    }    
		  });
		}
	}
  </script>
